  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_59565498-4b7b-425a-9205-27d07017c083'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2810236418467474364">All sorcerers are evil. Elisabeth has known that as long as she has known anything. Raised as a foundling in one of Austermeer’s Great Libraries, Elisabeth has grown up among the tools of sorcery—magical grimoires that whisper on shelves and rattle beneath iron chains. If provoked, they transform into grotesque monsters of ink and leather. She hopes to become a warden, cha</span>
  <span id="freeText2810236418467474364" style="display:none">All sorcerers are evil. Elisabeth has known that as long as she has known anything. Raised as a foundling in one of Austermeer’s Great Libraries, Elisabeth has grown up among the tools of sorcery—magical grimoires that whisper on shelves and rattle beneath iron chains. If provoked, they transform into grotesque monsters of ink and leather. She hopes to become a warden, charged with protecting the kingdom from their power.<br /><br />Then an act of sabotage releases the library’s most dangerous grimoire. Elisabeth’s desperate intervention implicates her in the crime, and she is torn from her home to face justice in the capital. With no one to turn to but her sworn enemy, the sorcerer Nathaniel Thorn, and his mysterious demonic servant, she finds herself entangled in a centuries-old conspiracy. Not only could the Great Libraries go up in flames, but the world along with them.<br /><br />As her alliance with Nathaniel grows stronger, Elisabeth starts to question everything she’s been taught—about sorcerers, about the libraries she loves, even about herself. For Elisabeth has a power she has never guessed, and a future she could never have imagined.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2810236418467474364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Sorcery of Thorns is intended for grades 9-12. It contains action-related violence and non-explicit kissing about on par with most young adult books. Your sister might enjoy it if she's an advanced reader, but I recommend reading it yourself first to determine whether the content is appropriate for her.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-sff">ya-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep-side">lgbtq-rep-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-bi">lgbtq-bi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569013875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8687236653195418043">Perhaps the cruelest and kindest thing a good book does is make you believe you live inside it for the space of a few hundred pages. That you are a part of something, part of its world, not just skating around the edges, too tied up in yourself to join in…and then it ends and the illusion winks out, like a snuffed flame, and you’re left marooned, adrift, your head chilled in its absence.<br/><br/>The real world takes a seat at the back, and Rogerson’s imaginary one holds center stage. Here where books are</span>
  <span id="freeText8687236653195418043" style="display:none">Perhaps the cruelest and kindest thing a good book does is make you believe you live inside it for the space of a few hundred pages. That you are a part of something, part of its world, not just skating around the edges, too tied up in yourself to join in…and then it ends and the illusion winks out, like a snuffed flame, and you’re left marooned, adrift, your head chilled in its absence.<br /><br />The real world takes a seat at the back, and Rogerson’s imaginary one holds center stage. Here where books are a soft warding from the beings that stalk the night and trapdoors to something beautiful and wicked that trickles beneath the surface, but when damaged—even inadvertently—they mutate into ravening monsters rising up in clamorous fury,  the warp spreading from the pages as sinuously as ink clouding through a glass of clean water. And they're called “Malefics.”<br /><br />The gist of the story concerns Elisabeth Scrivener who is an orphan raised in the Great library of Summershall where she learned the delicate arts of tending to books and the blunter arts of guarding them against the world, and guarding the world against them. Her apprenticeship as a warden was a sapling graft that barely had time to take when one night, Elisabeth wakes up to find the library’s Director slain and a Malefic free to loosen its wrath on her city. She takes the monster outright, vicious and victorious, with the strength of the Director’s sword, but before she could even begin to comprehend the magnitude of what had happened, Elisabeth is branded a murderer and a traitor, at only a word and a whim from the library’s new Director, and the charge of her punishment is given to the Magisterium.<br /><br />When the Great libraries start falling under attack, dread sluices through Elisabeth and a surety rises in her, lodging in her throat: someone is gathering arms against the Great libraries, colluding in treacheries, and, growing resigned to anyone believing her account, Elisabeth’s darkest self rises to the challenge: the heft of protecting the libraries would suit no one’s strength but hers—she who is “<em>a</em><em> true child of the library</em>”.<br /><br />But when secrets start melting into the dark, and all the doors slam shut in Elisabeth’s face, she seeks the help of Nathaniel Thorn, a sorcerer whose family is dogged with rumors of necromancy, and together they are soon yanked into the machinations of blood, greed and power. Revelations turn truths Elisabeth had known all her life into a tripwire primed to catch her off balance, and danger is dragged to her feet before she even sought it.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    Ink and parchment flowed through her veins. The magic of the Great Libraries lived in her very bones. They were a part of her, and she a part of them.
  </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Reading the first couple chapters, the strength of my delight, the speed with which it flowered, shocked me. <em>Sorcery of Thorns</em> burned through my initial skepticism, bright as a comet in the night’s sky, piercing me with vicious pleasure. In Rogerson’s luscious prose, <em>Sorcery of Thorns</em> weaves a pleasant spell indeed. This is a vibrant novel, and an unstintingly lush one. The author spins her tale with directness and wit; I enjoyed her storytelling, as one might enjoy music freely played, and was left clutching at each page as it slipped between my fingers.<br /><br />As familiar as the novel’s template is, Rogerson’s success lies in the way she infuses exhilarating new life into it through tenderly compelling characters, luxurious writing and an exquisitely wrought premise. It would be easy to say that it’s laden with genre tropes, but the author takes several classic fantasy stances and makes them seem utterly fresh on the page, and, though it occasionally dips in and out of cliché, the author never lets it linger there long. The result is an immensely immersive novel, as graceful and thoughtful as it is action-packed and pulse-pounding.<br /><br />Of course, no fantasy setting, however much entrancing and fresh it is, springs to life without strong characters to navigate it. On that end, <em>Sorcery of Thorns</em> delivers. The novel’s characters are engaging, and the relationships between them occupy the seething center of the sparsely ornamented stage.<br /><br />Elisabeth’s character takes on a magical aura all her own. Rogerson boldly, brilliantly places her protagonist at the center of a sprawling conflict, and with unremittent relish, she begins to undermine what Elisabeth understands about magic, grimoires, libraries, and her role in it. She challenges not only everything Elisabeth knows, but everything she has come to learn and think about herself. Elisabeth’s compelling blend of wide-eyed vulnerability and world-weary wryness anchors a deeply moving journey of self-realization.<br /><br />Elisabeth has never seen the world beyond the library where she grew up and tucked her dreams into her books for safekeeping. That her suspicions are so easily allayed first strained credulity, and I was often frustrated with how readily she settled into the words people dripped like sweet poison in her ear. But there was an edge to her, a keenness of anger and determination, and it soon strikes to life like flint. Elisabeth grows strong, unbent, scraping up all her fears and crushing them into an unlit place inside her. The <em>grimoires</em> called to her like signal beacons burning on a vast black sky and she flung herself into the air, fearless and unflinching. Elisabeth will protect the libraries like a mother wolf looking out for her cub, and she will not count the cost.<br /><br />Although the supporting cast of characters is not granted a vivacity as stark as Elisabeth’s, together they made a whole like the heart of a flame. <strong>Nathanial Thorn</strong> is rich, handsome, and beset by a tragic past. Not to mention: seductive toward men and women alike and blessed with a set of social graces that makes him look suave. Y’know…perfect daydream fodder. But Nathaniel is always alone, strangely solitary in the space everyone else gives him, and Elisabeth was acutely aware of the vast gulf between them: his fathomless barter with his unsettlingly taciturn servant, his tormented nightmares, the secrets she glimpsed only quickly through the corridors of his lonesome mansion; she wanted to shatter the cold mask of stone that Nathaniel slips down over himself in her presence, uncaring of how jagged and sharp he might be for her to cut herself on him.<br /><br />I liked Nathanial's character, but I was frankly far more intrigued by Silas and the inscrutable turning of his thoughts, like the cogs within a machine. Silas is Nathanial's silver-haired servant whose face was always a blank for just about any emotion one might care to project and who was a mystery, the safe Elisabeth (and the reader) could never crack, and I wanted to know if his icy exterior masks an even icier interior, or if it were a veneer for what was, at bottom, a warm and kind-hearted nature.<br /><br />If there’s a failing in <em>Sorcery of Thorns</em>, it’s that the ending is rushed in the novel’s last few chapters, and although a little light coruscating at the end of the tunnel is always a welcome respite, the conclusion felt a little too easy, too attainable, which knocked down some of my satisfaction. Minor quibble notwithstanding, <em>Sorcery of Thorns</em> is a remarkable achievement and I kind of hope the author writes more in this world.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    For these were not ordinary books the libraries kept. They were knowledge, given life. Wisdom, given voice. They sang when starlight streamed through the library’s windows. They felt pain and suffered heartbreak. Sometimes they were sinister, grotesque—but so was the world outside. And that made the world no less worth fighting for, because wherever there was darkness, there was also so much light.
  </em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8687236653195418043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer33100840363118414">I can't stop smiling. Margaret blows me away every time! <br/><br/>Sorcery of Thorns is equal parts whimsical, flirtatious, and totally hysterical, while still managing to deliver a gut-punch of feels on more than one occasion. This story is an absolute blast to read, and kept me thoroughly entertained all the way through.<br/><br/>First we have Elizabeth, a library apprentice of sorts. She's tall, fierce, yet has the gentlest of hearts. Time and time again, she charges headfirst into danger and drags us with her, </span>
  <span id="freeText33100840363118414" style="display:none">I can't stop smiling. Margaret blows me away every time! <br /><br />Sorcery of Thorns is equal parts whimsical, flirtatious, and totally hysterical, while still managing to deliver a gut-punch of feels on more than one occasion. This story is an absolute blast to read, and kept me thoroughly entertained all the way through.<br /><br />First we have Elizabeth, a library apprentice of sorts. She's tall, fierce, yet has the gentlest of hearts. Time and time again, she charges headfirst into danger and drags us with her, and her cleverness and willpower never disappoint. I'd follow her anywhere. Literally. <br /><br />Elizabeth's world is upheaved when a grimoire (yep you heard me) escapes the library. Mind you, grimoires are no ordinary books. In this world, they are quite alive with minds of their own - and can be very dangerous. Elizabeth, who's well aware of this danger, charges after it (of course, it isn't in 'book' form anymore and is now a rather grotesque lard-of-a-monster) to try and save her town from destruction. And while she succeeds (because she's a badass), she's accused of treason for letting it escape in the first place.<br /><br />Which means she's shipped off to who-knows-where, now in the charge of a sorcerer.<br /><br />Only, that sorcerer is Nathaniel and he's quite literally the best. <br /><br />But Elizabeth doesn't know that, and she certainly doesn't trust him (because sorcerers are evil apparently). And, typical Elizabeth isn't going to sit still while evil-hot-sorcerer-dude carts her away and disposes her body. Naturally, she tries to escape.<br /><br />But alas! Sorcerer dude Nathaniel isn't going to let her get away (though he'll roll his eyes a time or two because ugh she's impossible). And his butler, of all people, seems to have spooky-special powers that ensure Elizabeth fails in every attempt.<br /><br />So Elizabeth, our strong-willed heroine, is stuck with hawt and untrustworthy Nathaniel, and his creepy butler-friend-thing-who-clearly-has-powers.<br /><br />As usual, I'm not going to spoil much more, but suffice it to say, things don't go as planned. Because don't forget! Somehow that grimoire escaped. And if it wasn't Elizabeth, who was it? Ah! There is evil afoot, friends, and as I'd hoped, it forces Eizabeth and Nathaniel to team up and uproot it. <br /><br />Only, they may be over their heads. <br /><br />So I leave you with this: Make room in your hearts! We have on our hands a new story with gorgeous prose (as expected), absolute hysterical banter, new precious characters, and a riveting <b>hate-to-love ship</b>. I can't even pick what I love the most - the incredible world-building (omg can this be a movie?) or the brilliant prose. Or the characters, who are as real as they are fantastical. <br /><br />And! That! End!<br /><br />The last page. I actually gasped aloud and scared my cat. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.reverieandink.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>

<div id="review_2587164447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2587164447" />
    <a title="Margaret Rogerson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51907982-margaret-rogerson"><img alt="Margaret Rogerson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468069754p2/51907982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2587164447?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret Rogerson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret Rogerson" href="/user/show/51907982-margaret-rogerson">Margaret Rogerson</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)
          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43368595-sorcery-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2587164447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3164315040605457603">Hi, all! I don’t spend much time here (I view this as a place for readers, not me), but now that Sorcery of Thorns is appearing on people’s radars, I thought it would be a good opportunity to mention a couple of things.<br/><br/>Firstly: Sorcery is quite a different book than An Enchantment of Ravens, which may be helpful for readers to know in advance. Probably the best way to put it is that Enchantment is a fairy tale romance, while Sorcery is an epic fantasy. Sorcery does have a romance, but it’s a sub</span>
  <span id="freeText3164315040605457603" style="display:none">Hi, all! I don’t spend much time here (I view this as a place for readers, not me), but now that Sorcery of Thorns is appearing on people’s radars, I thought it would be a good opportunity to mention a couple of things.<br /><br />Firstly: Sorcery is quite a different book than An Enchantment of Ravens, which may be helpful for readers to know in advance. Probably the best way to put it is that Enchantment is a fairy tale romance, while Sorcery is an epic fantasy. Sorcery does have a romance, but it’s a subplot, not the main focus of the story. I had a ridiculous amount of fun writing it—and hope you enjoy venturing into this world’s perilous magical libraries alongside Elisabeth Scrivener. Sorcery is also a standalone book, completely unrelated to my previous novel.<br /><br />Secondly, I don’t believe Sorcery requires any major content warnings, but I’d like to run through a few possible triggers just in case. They are as follows:<br /><br />Body horror associated with the books-turned-monsters<br />Minor, brief self-injury when characters draw blood for magical rituals<br />Implied/referenced sexual assault (not graphic, nothing described on page)<br />Children disciplined using corporal punishment (think Dickens; again, not shown on page)<br />Victorian-era attitudes about mental health—hysteria, etc<br /><br />If you have any questions about these or want to know about any other specific potential triggers and/or page numbers, feel free to reach out me and I’ll get back to you ASAP! I’m going to vanish from Goodreads again after I post this, so please contact me on Twitter, Tumblr, or via the email address listed on my website.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3164315040605457603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2587164447">

<div id="review_2511786910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2511786910" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2511786910?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=z-2019-reads">z-2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=disability-and-mi">disability-and-mi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2511786910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1322531800750593530"><blockquote>
  <b>She wasn’t a wielder of chains; she was a breaker of them. She was the library’s will made flesh.</b>
</blockquote> <br/>I never do this, but I’m going to give you all a <b>TL;DR</b> for this review, just in case you’re in a hurry and need me to get the point across quickly: <b>
  <u>This is one of the <i>best</i> books I have read in my entire life, and if there is any single book I could beg you to purchase this year, it is <i>Sorcery of Thorns.</i></u>
</b> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b> “Knowledge always has the potential to be dangerous. It is a more powerful weapon tha</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1322531800750593530" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>She wasn’t a wielder of chains; she was a breaker of them. She was the library’s will made flesh.</b>
</blockquote> <br>I never do this, but I’m going to give you all a <b>TL;DR</b> for this review, just in case you’re in a hurry and need me to get the point across quickly: <b>
  <u>This is one of the <i>best</i> books I have read in my entire life, and if there is any single book I could beg you to purchase this year, it is <i>Sorcery of Thorns.</i></u>
</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b> “Knowledge always has the potential to be dangerous. It is a more powerful weapon than any sword or spell.”</b>
</blockquote><br>After adoring Margaret’s debut, <i>An Enchantment of Ravens,</i> it felt blaringly obvious that I would love this, too, but I had no idea how much my love for this world, this story, and these characters would blow <i>Enchantment</i> out of the water. The lore and world-building are so gorgeous and intricate, particularly surrounding the <b>grimoires.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Books, too, had hearts, though they were not the same as people’s, and a book’s heart could be broken; she had seen it happen before. Grimoires that refused to open, their voices gone silent, or whose ink faded and bled across the pages like tears.</b>
</blockquote><br>You see, you might know that this book is about books, and magic, and libraries, but what I loved most is that there are no simple <i>books</i> in <i>Sorcery.</i> Grimoires are living, feeling creatures, capable of good or bad, kindness or scorn, and most of all, of being corrupted. Elisabeth, having grown up in a library (literally), is more familiar than most with the grimoires, and her level of respect and adoration for them made me ache. As another adult who grew up with books as my closest friends, I loved how easily I related to her desperate need to be surrounded by books and to take care of them. (After all, it’s why I became a librarian, too!)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>For these were not ordinary books the libraries kept. They were knowledge, given life. Wisdom, given voice.</b>
</blockquote><br>Margaret’s care in crafting these grimoires is evident from the start, but as the story progresses, I was amazed at how important a piece of the story they became. I won’t spoil anything, but I will tell you that I have never in my life literally <i>sobbed</i> over a narrative about <i>books</i> in my life until this story.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b> “You belonged in the library, as much as any book.”</b>
</blockquote><br>Of course, that’s enough about the grimoires, because the primary star of the show is Elisabeth, and hell, she deserves an entire review dedicated solely to what an incredible, hilarious, witty, kind, lovable character she is. She’s clumsy and awkward in all the best ways, and she genuinely leaps right off the page with her general <i>realness</i>. There’s a sub-plot line involving her and the development of PTSD that felt so honest and authentic, it broke my heart for her every time it reared its head and made me root that much harder for her successes and happiness.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b> “Are all librarians like you, or is it only the feral ones who have been raised by booklice?”</b>
</blockquote><br>Sharing the spotlight is our love interest, the infamous, talented, handsome (and casually queer!) sorcerer Nathaniel, and his demon servant/companion Silas, either of whom I would happily protect at all costs because they are precious and not to be trifled with. Okay, Nathaniel could probably use a little trifling-with in his life, particularly because he responds with disarmingly hilarious nonchalance to every minor or major disaster Elisabeth drags him into. Silas, on the other hand… well, you’ll just have to meet him for yourself, but I don’t think anyone could <i>not</i> love his grouchy, quietly protective demonic self.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b> “It’s an honor to fight by your side, Elisabeth, for however long it lasts.”</b>
</blockquote><br>Oh, and I can’t pass up the opportunity to mention the <b>romance!</b> It’s fairly slow-burning, and it forms in the most natural, beautiful way. I loved watching Elisabeth and Nathaniel grow to trust one another, become friends, and gradually recognize the fact that neither of them could fathom this adventure without the other. If you all could see the number of tabs I used just on Nathaniel’s sweet admissions of affection, <i>wow.</i> I might have also tabbed every single instance in which Nathaniel called Elisabeth “you absolute menace”, because if that didn’t sum up their relationship as a whole, I don’t know what could have. My heart is so full.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>She felt as though she stood on a precipice, and that if she leaned forward, she would fall. She would fall, and drown with him; she would never resurface for air.</b>
</blockquote><br>Beyond all of this, the plot in this story is so engaging and suspenseful! I’d been reading <i>Sorcery</i> as slowly as I could stand to, because I knew I would be devastated when it ended, but once I hit the last hundred pages or so, I couldn’t be interrupted for anything because I simply <i>had</i> to know what happened next—and reader, let me tell you, not a single word in this story disappointed me. For every expectation I had of this book, Margaret surpassed it by a country mile.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b> “Of course you can stay, you menace. It isn’t as though I could stop you even if I wanted to. And fine, I’ll help you. Not for any noble reason. I still think it’s a lost cause. We’re probably going to get ourselves killed. But every man has his limits. If there’s one thing I can’t do, it’s stand by and watch you demolish irreplaceable antiques.”</b>
</blockquote><br>As you can see, from the fact that I’m forcing myself now to refrain from writing another entire page to this review about all of the things I adored in <i>Sorcery of Thorns,</i> I cannot recommend this book highly enough. It is easily my favorite read of 2019, and one of my favorite reads <i>of all time.</i> It touched my heart in a million places and a million ways I could never have predicted and will never fully recover from, frankly. I can’t wait to reread it over and over again, and more than that, I can’t wait to see what Margaret writes next.<br><br><i>All quotes come from an advance copy and may not match the final release. Thank you so much to the author for providing me with this ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543105511i/26644158.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1322531800750593530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2568552176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568552176" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2568552176?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=subscription-box-owlcrate">subscription-box-owlcrate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=subscription-box-fairyloot">subscription-box-fairyloot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=blog-tour">blog-tour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568552176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2862423714090877874"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555361252i/27367634._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by Simon & Schuster in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Knowledge always has the potential to be dangerous. It is a more powerful weapon than any sword or spell.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I don’t know about you, but I feel like I’ve been looking for a story all about someone living in a library, surrounded by magical books, while also going on adventure after adventure, for my entire life. And I truly believe that not only did Margaret Rogerson give me that, she is giving the YA literature communit</span>
  <span id="freeText2862423714090877874" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555361252i/27367634._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by Simon &amp; Schuster in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Knowledge always has the potential to be dangerous. It is a more powerful weapon than any sword or spell.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I don’t know about you, but I feel like I’ve been looking for a story all about someone living in a library, surrounded by magical books, while also going on adventure after adventure, for my entire life. And I truly believe that not only did Margaret Rogerson give me that, she is giving the YA literature community a gift from above. I feel like when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2040570555" rel="nofollow noopener">An Enchantment of Ravens</a> came out most people loved it, but it did seem a little bit polarizing, while I liked it but I never was in love with it. But <i>Sorcery of Thorns</i> captivated me from page one, and I adored it so very much that there was never a moment that I wanted to shut this very magical book and stop reading.<br><br>And like I said above, this is a story all about a girl named Elisabeth who has grown up in a library all of her life. She wants to eventually be a Warden, who is a person who protects the library, the people, and the books, because some books in this world are very much alive and are capable of doing some very bad things. But one night, when there is an attack at the library and the surrounding town, she takes it upon herself to defend the only home she has ever known. Yet, this act ends up making her the only suspect in the crime. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Dreadful things roam the shadows while the human world sleeps.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>So, Elisabeth gets sent away and is forced to travel alongside a nobleman and sorcerer named Nathaniel Thorn, who also has a companion named Silas who happens to be a demon. In this world, the old royal families have all made pacts with demons to give them magical powers, and these pacts are passed down from generation to generation, but at a cost. Also, Silas is easily my favorite character in this book and I would die for him this very instant. <br><br>But Elisabeth, Nathaniel, and Silas’s paths all continue to cross while Elisabeth is trying to prove her innocence, while also stumbling upon a conspiracy theory to end all other conspiracy theories about what is really happening to the libraries in this world. And the adventures they go on, the secrets they unfold, and the discoveries they make together, was nothing short of a treat to read. <br><br>The thing that I didn’t love about this book, and the reason I am giving it four stars, is because I didn’t love the very vague representation. Obviously, I want authors to write what they want to write and what they feel comfortable with, but this was a little too subtly done for me. Yes, we have a main character that does express attraction to more than one gender, which I am always going to be living for, but we get a very brushed off moment with a very minor character being on the ace spectrum. Also, I think another leading character could possibly also be on the ace spectrum, but the representation in this book is so quiet that you are constantly left second guessing yourself while reading, and it feels bad, even with the excuse that this story is set in a fantasy world because the mentions are so very brief, too. <br><br>Overall, I did love this story. It was so unique and so whimsical; I couldn’t resist getting completely swept off my feet. I loved all three characters and their dark backgrounds, while gaining so much hope for their futures. I loved the writing and all the twists and turns that this adventure packed story delivered. I loved the historical setting, which is very reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2465856942" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infernal Devices</a>! I loved the romance even though it was such a slow-burn that I wanted to scream in the best way possible! I just loved it all, and I can’t wait to see what Margaret Rogerson does next! Especially because this is a standalone, but I could totally see more in this world after that last page. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br><b>Content and Trigger Warnings:</b> anxiety depiction, anxiety attacks, talk of loss of a loved one, captivity, talk of forced institutionalization, and violence. <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/69919640-sol-thebookishking" rel="nofollow noopener">Sol</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4988733-alexa" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexa</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5524572-kristin-hackett-superspacechick" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristin</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12402009-alana-thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Alana</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="2862423714090877874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2807787128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2807787128" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2807787128?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2807787128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17289336283349835922">5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/08/11/sorcery-of-thorns-by-margaret-rogerson/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Most people grow out of fairy stories,” he said. “Why did you carry on believing, when the rest of the world did not?”<br/>“What is the point of life if you don’t believe in anything?” she asked instead.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Do you want some thoughts on this book? Imma give you some thoughts on this book. <b>I loved the hell out of it!</b><br/><br/>If you did not read this book, I tell you to do just that ASAP because I, too, have been sleeping on it for far too long and now I</span>
  <span id="freeText17289336283349835922" style="display:none">5/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/08/11/sorcery-of-thorns-by-margaret-rogerson/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Most people grow out of fairy stories,” he said. “Why did you carry on believing, when the rest of the world did not?”<br>“What is the point of life if you don’t believe in anything?” she asked instead.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Do you want some thoughts on this book? Imma give you some thoughts on this book. <b>I loved the hell out of it!</b><br><br>If you did not read this book, I tell you to do just that ASAP because I, too, have been sleeping on it for far too long and now I feel bad about it.<br><br>Thanks to one of my Goodreads friends I actually got to read it and I fell in love with it from the first chapters. Like, ugh, the spell this book has put on me was absolutely unbelievable. Too few books make me love them so briskly.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520476518ra/25179044.gif" width="331" height="246" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Let’s start with the basics.<br>I LOVE THE COVER.<br><br>You know me, with my endless fascination for covers. Well, this one is so beautiful and so aesthetically pleasing I just couldn’t help but mention its awesomeness.<br><br>Then, moving on to a more serious topic, I have to say that the <b>world</b> in this book is something very solid-looking, even though there are no elaborate passages depicting every inch of it. There are details thrown in here and there that help the reader make up the world like a puzzle, the final outcome being more than satisfactory. You only need a few names of places and a bit of history to make a world look real.<br><br>To me, <i>
  <b>Sorcery of Thorns</b>
</i> gives off such Harry Potter-ish vibes I couldn’t help but thoroughly enjoy! There is something in its essence theme, something tied to libraries and books and magic and knowledge, that just appealed to me. As a certified bookworm, I think this shouldn’t come as a surprise, but it is still nice to acknowledge it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Knowledge always has the potential to be dangerous. It is a more powerful weapon than any sword or spell.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>The fact that all those amazing, bookworm-ish elements get to tag along with some dark features like demon summoning just gives the whole atmosphere of the book a nice, cool breeze. <br><br>The <b>action</b> itself is very good. It flows and it is interesting to see how certain ideas are put into place and how are they going to turn out. With magic involved, one could never be more careful, am I right? Sorcery is unpredictable and so, it makes the plot a bit more complicated. Which is amazing because who likes a lame plot?<br><br>My favourite thing about this book though are the <b>characters.</b><br>Such amazingly lovable characters, only the devils bellow know how they can be this way. I felt a deep connection to them after just a few words uttered out of their mouths.<br><br><b>Elisabeth</b> is a total chaos, but I swear I love her. She is childish, but in a sweet way, and the fact that she is so fearless and so strong and tall just adds to the charm of her. But, seriously now, can we talk about the fact that tall girls in books are so underappreciated like for real, sisters do exist and they are some sort of goddesses too. As a 5’4’’ girl, all I can say that I admire tall girls from down here on the ground.<br><br>Elisabeth, you voice of tall and brave and sweet girls, you are a legend. And not only for that, but for the open-mindedness and courage you have.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“She now understood that the world wasn’t kind to young women, especially when they behaved in ways men didn’t like, and spoke truths that men weren’t ready to hear.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><b>Nathaniel</b> is a boy to melt for. He is supposed to be this fancy-ass sorcerer who sacrifices virgins and drinks their blood from a golden chalice every month with full moon, but in fact he is only a lonely boy.<br><br>He is so damn witty and he has this air about him that makes him funny in a way that is not goofy, but it’s sweet. There really is something about Nathaniel that made me categorise him as swoon-worthy, whether if it was his smart mouth or his confidence or his loyalty or his silver streak in his black hair, I don’t care. He is lovable.<br><br>And also, I don’t want to forget about <b>Silas.</b><br>Well, Silas is a demon I could die for. He’s too precious. And even though he really is a savage creature, soulless and selfish, he’s still a cute, fluffy kitten. I would kill for a friend like Silas.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551125956ra/27117739.gif" width="268" height="301" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I am actually super pleased with this book. And, honestly, I wanted more. It is a shame that it is only a standalone because I could definitely sense some other great adventure that might’ve taken place after all the action was done.<br><br>I think I might say that because I simply haven’t had enough of those amazingly lovable and adorable characters, but I do want to read more of them. There is a certain dose of addiction that I tasted and I am not done with.<br><br>All jokes aside, more Elisabeth, Nathaniel and Silas, please? It would mean the world to me, thanks.<br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591186026i/29587143._SX540_.jpg" width="340" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>@natt_lux_art<br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/64e135a0-0abd-4122-927e-57d46cbe418b_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="17289336283349835922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Margaret Rogerson is well on her way to becoming a new favourite author of mine. This was a follow-up novel done RIGHT. <br/><br/>RTC!</span>

<div id="review_2793944343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2793944343" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2793944343?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2833036994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16903935722490037098"><b>
  <i>‘for all the girls who found themselves in books.’</i>
</b><br/><br/>yaaassss! we stan a fantasy queen who both acknowledges AND writes stories for us bookworms. <3<br/><br/>i know i wont be the only reader who sees a little bit of themself in elisabeth; for being able to relate, on such a personal level, to her love of books, for seeing them as companions, and forever feeling at home in their company/in a library. <br/><br/>and this story is every bit deserving of having such a remarkable character. there is so much balance to t</span>
  <span id="freeText16903935722490037098" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘for all the girls who found themselves in books.’</i>
</b><br /><br />yaaassss! we stan a fantasy queen who both acknowledges AND writes stories for us bookworms. &lt;3<br /><br />i know i wont be the only reader who sees a little bit of themself in elisabeth; for being able to relate, on such a personal level, to her love of books, for seeing them as companions, and forever feeling at home in their company/in a library. <br /><br />and this story is every bit deserving of having such a remarkable character. there is so much balance to this story, that i honestly couldnt have asked for anything more. elisabeths fierce loyalty is a match for nathaniels charm and humour. the fast-paced plot is evened out with with meaningful scenes and narration. and the enchanting magic is made even more alluring with the personal growth and development of the characters because of it. <br /><br />this story is perfection for lovers of books and sorcery and i wouldnt have it any other way. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2986987029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2986987029" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/100759205-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603130096p2/100759205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2986987029?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/100759205-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986987029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15958755220445176356">OK HERE'S A BREAKDOWN:<br/><br/>stuff i liked:<br/>-just a really, genuinely fun read tbh. i honestly can't think of the last YA fantasy book that made me yELL the way this one did<br/>-silas, duh<br/>-nathaniel and elisabeth's relationship (separately, they were nothing special. but together?? delightful). I thought that enemies to lovers was executed well enough (even if it waaaas kinda fast, but anyway) AND Nathaniel was snarky and mysterious without being a complete asshole, which is *oh* so rare<br/><br/>stuff i disliked:<br/>-th</span>
  <span id="freeText15958755220445176356" style="display:none">OK HERE'S A BREAKDOWN:<br /><br />stuff i liked:<br />-just a really, genuinely fun read tbh. i honestly can't think of the last YA fantasy book that made me yELL the way this one did<br />-silas, duh<br />-nathaniel and elisabeth's relationship (separately, they were nothing special. but together?? delightful). I thought that enemies to lovers was executed well enough (even if it waaaas kinda fast, but anyway) AND Nathaniel was snarky and mysterious without being a complete asshole, which is *oh* so rare<br /><br />stuff i disliked:<br />-the convenience of the plot. they should all be dead, end of story. (if I was doing this review right I'd talk about how the lack of consequences as a result of this = boring read in respects to action and in a high fantasy book action is sorta kinda maybe important blah blah blah but let's just move on)<br />-the explanation of why elisabeth was so special was ??? not an explanation ?? also ????<br />-the writing def fell into that "trying to be pretty and lyrical so let's just say things that don't really make sense" category<br />-elisabeth's naivety throughout led to a lot of info-dump world building<br /><br />ultimately, it was an entertaining read, albeit a flawed one, so we're going with a 3/5. that may seem low given the hype that this book has received this year, but seeing as i DNF'd this author's debut 20 pages in and never looked back, i'd say this book showed great improvement :)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2843954409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2843954409" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2843954409?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=i-m-intrigued">i-m-intrigued</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2843954409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10382227568763974369">Nooo! Nooo! Nooo! It cannot end like this! This book urgently needs a sequel. All those amazing characters already stole my heart and grew on me that’s why I didn’t want to let them go.<br/><br/>There are too many things to adore about this story starting with a librarian heroine, Elizabeth who better connects with the magical world of books instead of forming a relationship with real humans. ( I agree to that book cannot make you pissed off so much and devastatingly break your heart! Okay, I’m taking bac</span>
  <span id="freeText10382227568763974369" style="display:none">Nooo! Nooo! Nooo! It cannot end like this! This book urgently needs a sequel. All those amazing characters already stole my heart and grew on me that’s why I didn’t want to let them go.<br /><br />There are too many things to adore about this story starting with a librarian heroine, Elizabeth who better connects with the magical world of books instead of forming a relationship with real humans. ( I agree to that book cannot make you pissed off so much and devastatingly break your heart! Okay, I’m taking back! Because they really can!) So Elizabeth naturally grew in this library and was raised by this book so eventually she felt like she needed to become the Warden, a devoted protector of the books. But unexpected attack to the library ruins her life. Not only her true home was affected by this merciless, violent attack, but also she was unfairly blamed by the town people.<br /><br />So as a punishment she was sent to a journey with a nobleman and a sorcerer. So we’re introduced our deliciously entertaining characters throughout this journey.<br /><br />But my most favorite character I truly fell for… what for it… a demon… SILAS is playful, smart, sarcastic, charming. And of course we have another charismatic character, NATHANIEL THORN ( fascinating, burned, complex, another sarcastic character) Eventually we witness the slow burn romance between Elizabeth and him. But as you may imagine I root for team Silas and I wish Elizabeth and him had their special romantic moments. (They could be controversial but interesting couple, don’t you think?)<br />Slow burn romance fit well with mysterious they encounter. Elizabeth tries to prove her innocence but as soon as she thinks she finds the true answer about what happens to those libraries in their world, another unexpected twist makes her stumble and trio’s ambition and determination to learn the secrets and find the truth hid behind the mysterious elements and their heart throbbing journey were memorable elements of the book. <br /><br />What I didn’t like it is the PACING. It was too fast and making you feel like you’re joining a fantasy book marathon. You start to connect and love those characters and you wish their journey could be longer. I expected this book is the first reading of a trilogy but well it’s gone with the wind. Flied away! Oh Silas,you deserve your own book sequel. Maybe I should start a campaign to convince the author to write more books about him because he definitely deserves more pages and I wanted to know more about his past and his future journeys.<br /><br />As a summary, I liked those characters’ way of facing their dark pasts and their strength to pass through the obstacles, their relationship dynamics, all those schemes and twists of the story worked really well with me. I am so happy to read debut work of a brilliant writer but I wish it could be a little slower, more detailed, longer. But I mostly enjoyed the writing and cannot wait to read more books of the author.<br /><br />P.S.: Please please please write more about Silas and name the book as “Irresistible Charm of Demon”!!! I guarantee that I could reread it over and over again!!!<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10382227568763974369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3218111084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1425162456212868383">(3.75) I haven't kept up with the new popular YA Fantasy but I decided to give this one a shot.<br/><br/>To be fair, I thought it was about fairies so... clearly I knew nothing about this.<br/><br/>Magical books, libraries, interesting enough story and characters. I didn't care much for the romance but let's be real, I rarely do and it wasn't overwhelming. The ending (well last quarter of the book) was weaker in my opinion but it was a light, quick and fun read.<br/><br/>If you usually enjoy YA Fantasy, give this one a shot!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2878197831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2878197831" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2878197831?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=full-five-stars">full-five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favs-of-2019">favs-of-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2878197831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6906763833721178933">THIS BOOK SAID TALL GIRL RIGHTS!!!! THIS BOOK SAID BISEXUAL RIGHTS!!!!!<br/><br/>Don't let this book fool you and let you think it's just another author trying to capitalize off of having the word "Thorns" in the title to appear like a Sarah J. Maas knock-off. This is my favorite book of 2019, and Sarah J. Maas should be SHAKING right now. I read this author's debut book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202169931?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Enchantment of Ravens,</a> and hated it, so I was skeptical going into it. But I knew within the first chapter of this book that it was </span>
  <span id="freeText6906763833721178933" style="display:none">THIS BOOK SAID TALL GIRL RIGHTS!!!! THIS BOOK SAID BISEXUAL RIGHTS!!!!!<br /><br />Don't let this book fool you and let you think it's just another author trying to capitalize off of having the word "Thorns" in the title to appear like a Sarah J. Maas knock-off. This is my favorite book of 2019, and Sarah J. Maas should be SHAKING right now. I read this author's debut book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202169931?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">An Enchantment of Ravens,</a> and hated it, so I was skeptical going into it. But I knew within the first chapter of this book that it was going to be something else entirely on a whole different level, and it was. The glow up this author went through, in my opinion, is UNREAL.<br /><br />The writing style? STUNNING<br />The characters? BRILLIANT<br />The romance? SOFT<br />The plot? I'M RUNNING OUT OF ADJECTIVES<br /><br />When I say this book is unique, I don't mean it's ~special~ or it's ~interesting~. I mean there is literally not a single book out there that has done what this book has done. It has the cozy, library vibe of Harry Potter. It has the demonic tinge and 19th century flare of The Infernal Devices. It has the magical angst of a Sarah J. Maas book. And yet it did all of that together flawlessly, and better than all the previous series combined.<br /><br />I adored the main character, who was a wallflower and quiet but also had a side of her that was fiercely loyal, honest, and willing to question injustice. I'm always a sucker for characters who fight to do good despite their circumstances, and Elisabeth definitely embodied that. I particularly loved her because SHE SUFFERS FROM PANIC ATTACKS!!! and yet is a smart, badass heroine. Also, she is described as being tall and that fact is very present in the book, and it made my tall girl heart soar!! Nathaniel was also a dynamic character who both filled the role of sassy, broody, BISEXUAL!!!!! love interest but was also an entire person on his own with a lineage and backstory that speaks a lot to his development. Them together was such an interesting pair and would I have complained if we got more smut? Absolutely not.<br /><br /><br />For the majority of this book, I did not have a single complaint. It was gripping with everyone scene flowing seamlessly to the next. I adored every side character. The writing was magnificent and awe-inspiring; flowery without being too self-important. The characters jumped off the page and had realistic moral complexities. Typing this review, I feel like my fingers can't move fast enough to list its good qualities. But the one part (literally, the single only thing) that I wish this book were stronger about was the development of the villain. The main character discovers very quickly who is behind all of the nefarious activities going on, and from there, it's a pretty straight line to preventing that person from succeeding in their great plans. Although I feel the magical and political conflict was developed well, I wish the villain's side of the story were better explained or maybe even reworked to be less generic because the evil they were stopping was massive, and yet it felt like the reason that evil was being provoked was something quite basic and irrelevant. <br /><br />But despite that small grievance, I will be camping out on this author's doorstep for a sequel. I know it's a standalone, but these characters and this world have captured my heart and I refuse to let go. Wow, wow, wow, wow, wow. I don't have a good enough parting line to leave you with other than this is going to be my obsession for a very long time and I will stop at nothing to insist you all read it immediately.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6906763833721178933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2860988666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2860988666" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2860988666?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2860988666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5221774669088123722">I was wondering why I found myself underwhelmed throughout reading this book and I realize that it might be because I prefer Rogerson to write short, simple, romantic stories rather than trying to make a complex fantasy narrative. I appreciate the unique concept and world that she tried to convey, but I think there was a disconnect between that and the actual execution. I was aware of her intentions with the whimsical world building, snarky love interest, secretly soft demon, etc. but it didn’t </span>
  <span id="freeText5221774669088123722" style="display:none">I was wondering why I found myself underwhelmed throughout reading this book and I realize that it might be because I prefer Rogerson to write short, simple, romantic stories rather than trying to make a complex fantasy narrative. I appreciate the unique concept and world that she tried to convey, but I think there was a disconnect between that and the actual execution. I was aware of her intentions with the whimsical world building, snarky love interest, secretly soft demon, etc. but it didn’t impact me as intended. There were several times throughout the book where I found myself dragging to get through the unnecessarily long story and felt bogged down by it. There was no romantic chemistry between the couple at all, and the villain is one-dimensional and mustache-twirling. There are merits to this book and I appreciate the effort to create a unique type of fantasy story, but this wasn’t for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5221774669088123722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2890701213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2890701213" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2890701213?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=bookstagram-made-me-do-it">bookstagram-made-me-do-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2890701213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14786458509345222294">I'm so bummed, because I had a paper where I noted my favorite quotes and corresponding page numbers tucked into my hardcopy of this book, but I seem to have misplaced it. 😿 No matter, I will carry on and you will now know that I had so many quotes I loved from this book and there simply wasn't enough room here to include them. <br/><br/><b>Me, rushing to tell you all about this book:</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563816758ra/27869117.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sometimes, I think the entire experience surrounding a book contributes to our giving it 5 stars, rather than just the story i</span>
  <span id="freeText14786458509345222294" style="display:none">I'm so bummed, because I had a paper where I noted my favorite quotes and corresponding page numbers tucked into my hardcopy of this book, but I seem to have misplaced it. 😿 No matter, I will carry on and you will now know that I had so many quotes I loved from this book and there simply wasn't enough room here to include them. <br><br><b>Me, rushing to tell you all about this book:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563816758ra/27869117.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sometimes, I think the entire experience surrounding a book contributes to our giving it 5 stars, rather than just the story itself and my experience with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42201395.Sorcery_of_Thorns" title="Sorcery of Thorns by Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">Sorcery of Thorns</a> is a perfect example of this. Picture with me, a woman who is technically in Barnes and Noble shopping for her daughter, but clearly must snoop around, lest she miss any new releases, and stumbles upon a cover she has seen on numerous occasions, but never took the time to read the synopsis. I thought it sounded good, the cover was stunning, and after seeing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3030788-melanie" rel="nofollow noopener">Meltotheany</a> gave this one the green light, I did something I haven't done in <b>years</b>: I bought the dang book and started reading it the moment I got home. 😮 I'm so used to drowning in ARCs and not picking up a book until months or YEARS later, that this simple act was revolutionary to my reading slump. Long story short, my new goal is to get to a place where 75% of my reading is done in this manner. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563817375ra/27869140.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What's this book about? Glad you asked! It's about magical libraries, and the humans who protect the books that populate these sacred buildings. It's about sorcerers and demons, and a girl's journey on discovering how everything she's ever known may not be the gospel truth. It's about a journey to save the world from unparalleled evil, but also a journey in one's finding their self. It's romantic and inclusive and did I mention it features one of my favorite antiheroes of all time? This blubbering mess of a paragraph probably doesn't help you in figuring out exactly what this book is, but I'd rather leave it up to you to read for yourself. If you enjoy character driven fantasy with a wispy, slow building romance, noteworthy platonic relationships, and a diverse cast that doesn't feel included solely to be politically correct, you may enjoy this book as well. Also? I hope you love Silas as much as I did. 💖</span>
  <a data-text-id="14786458509345222294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
